<UserId.>113469649534788824819<//UserId.><Name>Drew Foster< /Name><date>1524760158755<//date><rate>5<//rate><review>If you had a picture in your mind of a typical neighborhood Irish pub then this is it. Most bars like this only take cash, but even though they still use one of those cool really old push button ding registers they actually have a card processor thingy too. The bartender if friendly and helpful when asking about nearby eateries. Now, about the bar tools who hold up the end of the bar to keep it from falling, well they are the part of what makes a local watering hole fun. The conversations and comical pokes n jabs as new old customers come n go is as much fun as watching your favorite late night show. Drop by have a drink and just listen, at some point maybe you'll have something to add and be able to get in on the fun. Best place in town to experience true Irish sunblock ;-)</review>< pics>

< review>
Like a going to a bar with a cute bartender with an Irish accent?!?
Then BOOM! Here ya go!
This place was a lot of fun! I came here to watch the basketball finals and had some friends meet up with me later. Yes, I went to a bar by myself and unlike another review here I did not get harassed. The people there were really nice and the bar mascot, a dog (whose name I cannot remember), is super friendly! We played music on the joke box later and had a couple rounds of drinks. It was really fun and not that expensive.
There is a pool table upstairs but I never ventured up there to play.
Overall, not a bad spot to hang out and I heard they will also have the NFL Sunday Ticket again this year!<//review>

< Text>
Looked this spot up before coming to Pismo for a staycation and glad I did. There's a plethora of spots in downtown Pismo by the pier that...aren't...incredibly...........diverse....in their offerings. Everyone has sides, burgers, boozy beverages, and their own version of clam chowder but Moreno's has incredibly flavorful Mexican fare, GREAT service, and a simple menu that's not trying to be more than what it is supposed to be.
I had a shrimp quesadilla; my wife had a breakfast burrito, and both were devoured within minutes of receiving them.
I needed more and ordered a barbacoa taco and an asada taco...both delicious and washed down with a Jarritos.
Clean joint with great food and friendly service.....what more does anyone need? Definitely returning the next time we are in town.< /Text>

<user_id>102280116513485317662<//user_id><name>James Papeika< /name>< Date>
1565492115482<//Date>
<Rate>5< /Rate><review>Fantastic overall experience!

I know there are already a lot of good reviews, but I will add one more. I assume that many of you, like me, appreciate a review with a little detail.

I did the two day (with camping) South Fork American River trip. This trip included lunch on both days. You will probably be very pleasantly surprised at the effort they put into the lunch. One day was a great lunch meat spread with onions, lettuce, tomatoes, pickles, and four or five breads. As an appetizer, which was swerved while the River guides sliced veggies and setup, they served chips, honey crisp apple slices, and orange slices. Day two was delicious taco salad. Both days included cold water and cookies too.

They cooked breakfast on day two also. Eggs, bacon, and both blueberry and chocolate chip pancakes. Of course, coffee and juice too.

On day one, they guides cooked dinner, which was a tasty chicken and pasta dish. Some adult beverages were also provided.

The rafting experience was excellent. The guides really make the trip better, and in my case, our guide Evan was wonderful. He worked really hard to make sure we enjoyed our trip. On day two, we ‚Äúsurfed‚Äù Chili Bar, which was thrilling. Evan had to work hard (three tries, and he had to jump in the River to move the boat) to get our boat in this unique current.

They are very safety conscious: a good briefing, flotation devices, and a helmet. Also, you will practice basic safety commands on the river.

The rafting itself was very exciting. Especially on day one, the rapids are fun without feeling overwhelming.  I voluntarily went for a swim at one point‚Äîyes the water is cold!

The final rapid on day 2, ‚ÄúTroublemaker,‚Äù was without a doubt the most intimidating, but with a good, well-trained guide (OARS has their guides complete weeks of training before they lead customers down the river), you will be safe.  If you are worried about falling out involuntarily, it of course could happen if Mother Nature decides she wants to rock the boat hard enough, but no one on my crew fell out.

One of the kids said it‚Äôs like an ride/water park, but on a real river instead of some amusement park. I like this analogy.

Day one was 4-5 hours, including lunch. Day two was 2-3 hours, including lunch. They did a good job with the schedule. Day two is more thrilling, but that‚Äôs fine because you learn and gain confidence after day one. Note: you can do a day trip for either day one or two‚Äîday two includes the Chili Bar and Troublemaker rapids, day 1 includes rapids like ‚ÄúSatan‚Äôs cesspool.‚Äù

For the camping, we paid a little extra for the platform tent. This setup was perfect‚Äîclean, roomy tent with two beds and a porch. If you like relaxing in the evening while camping, you will enjoy this setup. I did not need to bring any of my own camping gear. They also provide bathrooms and showers (you need your own toiletries and towels).  I guess this is really glampimg, given that someone cooked my meals!

At the end of each rafting day, they had ice cold sodas waiting. This seems like a silly thing to mention, but, after hours in the sun paddling, the soda was the prefect touch and highlights their focus on the customer experience.

I hope to do an OARS trip in the future.

I highly recommend if you are looking for an ‚Äúadventure‚Äù vacation. Our trip included kids, and I think this trip is kid-friendly (but they do need to be able to swim). if you are unsure, day one is less intimidating.

There are maybe 10 competitors‚ÄîOARS in my opinion is the best option (after seeing the other boats and facilities and lunch etc).  Everyone I spoke with, from scheduling to the campsite to the rafting, was personable and friendly.

Again, the guide Evan went above-and-beyond.  We learned a lot, talked during the calm water, and really enjoyed ourselves.

Final note: please remember the guides work in the service industry. Please tip them for their effort!<//review>< pics>

<time>1556946515600< /time><userid>118425622995986720908<//userid><gmap_id>0x80c2bb8c70df8313:0x282056364f2757c2</gmap_id><review>Went there with a client of mine tonight for dinner. The food was good - good enough I would come back (I had the Karp... whatever salad, and since my name is Karp, I just had to take it ;-).

The waiter - a big greek guy - cared enough to come, introduce himself and rattled down today's specials in a way he did not really care if we understood him or not and then.... ignored us. He passed us many times, we tried to get his attention again, no luck. After more than 20 minutes I eventually managed to get some other waiter to take our order.

It was really obvious that the waiter did not care and I would have possibly said something there, but as I said I was with a client - a big songwriter who traveled the world - and I did not want to spoil the evening.

Would I go again? Maybe - a very maybe and only with friends with a high tolerance for less than mediocre service. So sorry, even though the food we had was god (not very good, my chicken was dry), I want to stick with my consisent rating scheme and so three stars are the most I can give.

Thanks for reading my comment. Now, if you are curious enough about my "rating scheme", here's "the moment of truth. I am a music photographer who travels the world with the worlds greatest musical talents (Michael Jackson, AC/DC, Rolling Stones or Rammstein, to name a few) for almost 40 years. When being asked "where do you live" I tended to ask "in hotels". At my peak, I "shot" 250 shows a year. Will say: been there, saw and tasted it, and a lot, as I may say and much to the dismay of my doctor who is in my back to lose a few pounds. Quite a few, as I may add, which is why my wife and I walk ten thousand steps per day, where- and whenever we can - and explore a lot of new exciting places - places you may oversee when just driving by.

While I love to share my experience with others, I am sometimes shocked how people use their "power of word" to down-rate amazing places because of minor incidents (in my all time favourite restaurant Le Petit Four on Sunset Plaza the owner was even called a racist as he refused to toast the (free) bread in his packed restaurant - they simply do not offer toasted bread, as no French place does, as I may add). Or I just read "Chicken piccata so over-salted I hope the dog enjoys the leftovers tomorrow, I brought home most of the dish." Did they speak to their service? How could the restaurant learn that something was wrong when patrons even have their leftovers boxed to take home? As a dog owner, I want to take the writer and shake him or her really bad and say "you give over-salted food to your dog? Anyone with a bit of brain understands this is a horrible idea... I hope you agree.

So If I had the say on this portal, I would offer just to see ratings of my friends. So I would see what the ratings were by like-minded people. Sadly, I have no say. I try not to compare apples with oranges. A place like this simply does not compare to "The Ritz". At first, I assume that a restaurant is clean, they do not greet you with a gun - and they deliver whatever they promise. I do not give stars for things that are expected. In my rating scheme, three or more stars are awarded if they actually exceeded my expectation. Four, if I am sure I will come back. To achieve five stars, I must be willing to take a detour of thirty minutes or more to go again.

Thank you for reading this.< /review><response>None< /response>< Name>

<Date>1610393964034<//Date><userid>116584340640767932766<//userid>< Review>
Overall, this place is amazing & a MUST-GO when in Pismo!

Breakfast Burrito: a lot of reviews say that they have THE BEST breakfast burritos. That is a bold statement, but coming from someone who used to always get breakfast burritos, this is the best one I have every purchased. I think it has to do with being able to have your eggs however you want, so I got over-medium. Also, they use tater tots instead of chopped potatoes which is amazing.

It also comes with potatoe chips & salsa, all of which are good.

Southwest Wrap: more of a burrito tbh, but very good! Comes with curly fries.

There are plenty of places to eat outside, also you can see them grilling meat outside which shows that they care about quality.</Review>

<Date>1548227600941<//Date><Rating>5<//Rating>< Text>
I absolutely love Hoagie's! They have something for everyone on their menu. From clam chowder in a sourdough bread bowl (in which you can add multiple toppings like bacon, cheese, a crab and shrimp mixture and more!), wraps, tacos, sandwiches... The list goes on. Kid's meals come with curly fries and a drink in a cute reusable cup. The island smoothie was on point if you like mango and coconut.  I love that they also serve Peet's coffee! The black and white mocha is a personal fave of mine. They have a non-alcoholic Strawberry Refresher drink that is delicious! Their hot Turkey sandwich was tasty too! The people who work there are friendly and provide excellent service.< /Text>

< text>
Okay now that I watched this place evolve - I've found that they have stepped up their game. I found a new menu along with smoother operation.

Lines can still be long but that has to be indicative of the quality of food being served.

I would describe Hoagies as Surfer meets broke collage student who meets a stoner and they started tinkering in the kitchen. Off the hook tri-tip with fries and bbq sauce rolled in a tortilla wrap equals laid back great food.

Laid back atmosphere with great food has won my heart over. Keep up the great work.< /text>
